<p><b>Baku</b> (<a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_language" title="Azerbaijani language">Azerbaijani</a>: <span lang="az"><i>Bakı</i></span>, <small>IPA: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Turkic_dialects" title="Help:IPA for Turkic dialects">[bɑˈcɯ]</a></span>) is the capital and largest city of <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, as well as the largest city on the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> and of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> region. Baku is located 28 metres (92 ft) below <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a>, which makes it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_capital_cities_by_altitude" title="List of capital cities by altitude">lowest lying national capital in the world</a> and also the largest city in the world located below sea level. It is located on the southern shore of the <a href="/wiki/Absheron_Peninsula" title="Absheron Peninsula">Absheron Peninsula</a>, alongside the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Baku" title="Bay of Baku">Bay of Baku</a>. At the beginning of 2009, Baku's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urban_population" title="Urban population">urban population</a> was estimated at just over two million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pop_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-pop-5">[5]</a></sup> Officially, about 25 percent of all inhabitants of the country live in Baku's <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a>.</p>
<p>Baku is divided into <a href="/wiki/Baku#Administrative_divisions" title="Baku">eleven administrative districts</a> (raions) and 48 townships. Among these are the townships on the islands of the <a href="/wiki/Baku_Archipelago" title="Baku Archipelago">Baku Archipelago</a>, and the town of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_Rocks" title="Oil Rocks">Oil Rocks</a> built on stilts in the Caspian Sea, 60 kilometres (37 miles) away from Baku. The <a href="/wiki/Old_City_(Baku)" title="Old City (Baku)">Inner City</a> of Baku, along with the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_the_Shirvanshahs" title="Palace of the Shirvanshahs">Shirvanshah's Palace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maiden_Tower_(Baku)" title="Maiden Tower (Baku)">Maiden Tower</a>, were inscribed as a UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> in 2000. According to the <a href="/wiki/Lonely_Planet" title="Lonely Planet">Lonely Planet</a>'s ranking, Baku is also among the world's top ten destinations for urban nightlife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nl_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-nl-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city is the scientific, cultural and industrial center of Azerbaijan. Many sizeable Azerbaijani institutions have their headquarters there. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baku_International_Sea_Trade_Port" title="Baku International Sea Trade Port">Baku International Sea Trade Port</a> is capable of handling two million tons of general and dry bulk cargoes per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> In recent years, Baku has become an important venue for international events. It hosted the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2012" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2012">57th Eurovision Song Contest</a> in 2012, the <a href="/wiki/2015_European_Games" title="2015 European Games">2015 European Games</a>, the 2016 <a href="/wiki/European_Grand_Prix" title="European Grand Prix">European Grand Prix</a> and will host the 4th <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Solidarity_Games" title="Islamic Solidarity Games">Islamic Solidarity Games</a> in 2017 and <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2020" title="UEFA Euro 2020">UEFA Euro 2020</a>.</p>
<p>The city is renowned for its harsh winds, which is reflected in its nickname, the "<a href="/wiki/City_of_Winds" title="City of Winds">City of Winds</a>".</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Baku is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> name of the city باد-کوبه <i>Bād-kube</i>, meaning "Wind-pounded city", in which <i>bād</i> means "wind" and <i>kube</i> is rooted in the verb کوبیدن <i>kubidan</i>, "to pound", thus referring to a place where wind is strong and pounding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Web.archive.org_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Web.archive.org-8">[8]</a></sup> Indeed, the city is renowned for its fierce winter snow storms and harsh winds. This is also reflected in the city's nickname as the "<a href="/wiki/City_of_Winds" title="City of Winds">City of Winds</a>". A less probable <a href="/wiki/Folk_etymology" title="Folk etymology">folk etymology</a> explains the name as deriving from <i>Baghkuy</i>, meaning "God's town". <i>Baga</i> (now <i>بغ</i> <i>bagh</i>) and <i>kuy</i> are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Persian_language" title="Old Persian language">Old Persian</a> words for "god" and "town" respectively; the name <i>Baghkuy</i> may be compared with <i><a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdād</a></i> ("God-given") in which <i>dād</i> is the Old Persian word for "give". <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> sources refer to the city as <i>Baku</i>, <i>Bakukh</i>, <i>Bakuya</i>, and <i>Bakuye</i>, all of which seem to come from a Persian name.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Baku" title="History of Baku">History of Baku</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Baku" title="Timeline of Baku">Timeline of Baku</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antiquity">Antiquity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Antiquity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Qobustan_inscription.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Qobustan_inscription.jpg/220px-Qobustan_inscription.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Qobustan_inscription.jpg/330px-Qobustan_inscription.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Qobustan_inscription.jpg/440px-Qobustan_inscription.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Qobustan_inscription.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Roman stone inscription in <a href="/wiki/Gobustan_National_Park" title="Gobustan National Park">Gobustan</a> dating back to 84–96 A.D.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Around 100,000 years ago, the territory of modern Baku and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Absheron_Rayon" title="Absheron Rayon">Absheron</a> was <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savanna</a> with rich flora and fauna. Traces of human settlement go back to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stone_age" title="Stone age">Stone age</a>. From the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bronze_age" title="Bronze age">Bronze age</a> there have been rock carvings discovered near Bayil, and a bronze figure of a small fish discovered in the territory of the Old City. These have led some to suggest the existence of a Bronze Age settlement within the city's territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Near <a href="/wiki/Nardaran" title="Nardaran">Nardaran</a>, in a place called Umid Gaya, a prehistoric observatory was discovered, where on the rock the images of sun and various constellations are carved together with a primitive astronomic table.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Further archeological excavations revealed various prehistoric settlements, native temples, statues and other artifacts within the territory of the modern city and around it.</p>
<p>In the 1st century, the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a> organized two Caucasian campaigns and reached Baku. Near the city, in <a href="/wiki/Gobustan_National_Park" title="Gobustan National Park">Gobustan</a>, Roman inscriptions dating from 84–96 AD were discovered. This is one of the earliest written evidences for Baku.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_of_the_Shirvanshahs_and_the_Safavid_era">Rise of the Shirvanshahs and the Safavid era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Rise of the Shirvanshahs and the Safavid era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Shirvanshah" title="Shirvanshah">Shirvanshah</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1541-Battle_in_the_war_between_Shah_Isma%27il_and_the_King_of_Shirvan-Shahnama-i-Isma%27il.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1300" data-file-width="1000" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/1541-Battle_in_the_war_between_Shah_Isma%27il_and_the_King_of_Shirvan-Shahnama-i-Isma%27il.jpg/170px-1541-Battle_in_the_war_between_Shah_Isma%27il_and_the_King_of_Shirvan-Shahnama-i-Isma%27il.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/1541-Battle_in_the_war_between_Shah_Isma%27il_and_the_King_of_Shirvan-Shahnama-i-Isma%27il.jpg/255px-1541-Battle_in_the_war_between_Shah_Isma%27il_and_the_King_of_Shirvan-Shahnama-i-Isma%27il.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/1541-Battle_in_the_war_between_Shah_Isma%27il_and_the_King_of_Shirvan-Shahnama-i-Isma%27il.jpg/340px-1541-Battle_in_the_war_between_Shah_Isma%27il_and_the_King_of_Shirvan-Shahnama-i-Isma%27il.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1541-Battle_in_the_war_between_Shah_Isma%27il_and_the_King_of_Shirvan-Shahnama-i-Isma%27il.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Miniature_(illuminated_manuscript)" title="Miniature (illuminated manuscript)">miniature painting</a> marking the downfall of the Shirvanshahs at the hands of the Safavids.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the 8th century Baku was the realm of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shirvanshahs" title="Shirvanshahs">Shirvanshahs</a>. The city frequently came under assault of the <a href="/wiki/Khazars" title="Khazars">Khazars</a> and (starting from the 10th century) the <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus'">Rus</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Akhsitan_I_ibn_Minuchihr_III" title="Akhsitan I ibn Minuchihr III">Shirvanshah Akhsitan I</a> built a navy in Baku and successfully repelled another Rus assault in 1170. After a devastating earthquake struck <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shamakhy" title="Shamakhy">Shamakhy</a>, the capital of <a href="/wiki/Shirvan" title="Shirvan">Shirvan</a>, Shirvanshah’s court moved to Baku in 1191.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sabayil_relics.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1365" data-file-width="2048" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Sabayil_relics.jpg/220px-Sabayil_relics.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Sabayil_relics.jpg/330px-Sabayil_relics.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Sabayil_relics.jpg/440px-Sabayil_relics.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sabayil_relics.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Relics from the sunken <a href="/wiki/Sabayil_Castle" title="Sabayil Castle">Sabayil Castle</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Shirvan era greatly influenced Baku and the remainder of Azerbaijan. Between the 12th and 14th centuries, massive fortifications were undertaken in Baku and the surrounding towns. The <a href="/wiki/Maiden_Tower_(Baku)" title="Maiden Tower (Baku)">Maiden Tower</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ramana_Tower" title="Ramana Tower">Ramana Tower</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nardaran_Fortress" title="Nardaran Fortress">Nardaran Fortress</a>, the Shagan Castle, the <a href="/wiki/Quadrangular_castle_(Mardakan)" title="Quadrangular castle (Mardakan)">Mardakan Castle</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Round_Castle_(Mardakan)" title="Round Castle (Mardakan)">Round Castle</a> and also the famous <a href="/wiki/Sabayil_Castle" title="Sabayil Castle">Sabayil Castle</a> on the island of the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Baku" title="Bay of Baku">Bay of Baku</a> was built during this period. The <a href="/wiki/Old_City_(Baku)" title="Old City (Baku)">city walls of Baku</a> were also rebuilt and strengthened.</p>
<p>By the early 16th century Baku's wealth and strategic position attracted the focus of its larger neighbors, and had already been ruled in the previous two centuries by then in Iran centred <a href="/wiki/Kara_Koyunlu" title="Kara Koyunlu">Kara Koyunlu</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ak_Koyunlu" title="Ak Koyunlu">Ak Koyunlu</a>. The fall of the Ak Koyunlu brought the city immediately into the sphere of the newly formed Iranian <a href="/wiki/Safavid_dynasty" title="Safavid dynasty">Safavid dynasty</a>, who, led by <a href="/wiki/Ismail_I" title="Ismail I">Shah Ismail I</a> laid siege to Baku in 1501 and captured it making it an integral part of his empire and the successive Iranian dynasties to come for the next centuries, until the irrevocable cession in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Gulistan" title="Treaty of Gulistan">first half of the 19th century</a>. The House of Shirvan, who ruled Baku since the 9th century, was extinguished in the course of the Safavid rule.</p>
<p>At this time the city was enclosed within the lines of strong walls, which were washed by the sea on one side and protected by a wide trench on land. In 1540 Baku was again captured by the Safavid troops following a brief occupation by the Ottomans as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chaldiran" title="Battle of Chaldiran">Battle of Chaldiran</a>. In 1578 the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottomans</a> captured Baku and held it till 1603, when it was again put under Iranian control,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> under which it stayed, intermittently, up to <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Gulistan" title="Treaty of Gulistan">the course of the 19th century</a>. In 1604 the Baku fortress was destroyed by Shah <a href="/wiki/Abbas_I_of_Persia" title="Abbas I of Persia">Abbas I</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Downfall_of_the_Safavids_and_the_Khanate_of_Baku">Downfall of the Safavids and the Khanate of Baku</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Downfall of the Safavids and the Khanate of Baku">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The fall of the Iranian Safavids gave rise to the various <a href="/wiki/Khanates_of_the_Caucasus" title="Khanates of the Caucasus">Caucasian khanates</a>, most of whom were already established in the late Safavid era while the rest were established during the rule of Iranian ruler <a href="/wiki/Nader_Shah" title="Nader Shah">Nader Shah</a>. After the death of Nader Shah in 1747, the semi-independent Persian-ruled<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> principality of the <a href="/wiki/Baku_Khanate" title="Baku Khanate">Baku Khanate</a> was formed. It was ruled by Mirza Muhammed Khan but soon became a dependency of the much stronger <a href="/wiki/Quba_Khanate" title="Quba Khanate">Quba Khanate</a>. During the time, the population of Baku was small (approximately 5,000), and the economy was ruined as a result of constant warfare.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russo-Persian_Wars_and_Iran.27s_forced_ceding">Russo-Persian Wars and Iran's forced ceding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Russo-Persian Wars and Iran's forced ceding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%91%D0%B0%D0%BA%D1%83._%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F._1861.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="994" data-file-width="1600" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/%D0%91%D0%B0%D0%BA%D1%83._%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F._1861.jpg/220px-%D0%91%D0%B0%D0%BA%D1%83._%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F._1861.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/%D0%91%D0%B0%D0%BA%D1%83._%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F._1861.jpg/330px-%D0%91%D0%B0%D0%BA%D1%83._%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F._1861.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/%D0%91%D0%B0%D0%BA%D1%83._%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F._1861.jpg/440px-%D0%91%D0%B0%D0%BA%D1%83._%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F._1861.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%91%D0%B0%D0%BA%D1%83._%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F._1861.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Painting of Baku's shoreline in 1861 by <a href="/wiki/Alexey_Bogolyubov" title="Alexey Bogolyubov">Alexey Bogolyubov</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 26 June 1723, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1722%E2%80%9323)" title="Russo-Persian War (1722–23)">after a long siege</a>, Baku surrendered to the Russians and the Safavids were forced to cede the city alongside many other of their Caucasian territories as confirmed in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Saint_Petersburg_(1723)" title="Treaty of Saint Petersburg (1723)">1723 Saint Petersburg Treaty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> By 1730, the situation had deteriorated for the Russians as <a href="/wiki/Nader_Shah" title="Nader Shah">Nadir Shah's</a> successes in Shirvan forced the Russians to make an <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Ganja" title="Treaty of Ganja">agreement</a> near <a href="/wiki/Ganja,_Azerbaijan" title="Ganja, Azerbaijan">Ganja</a> on 10 March 1735, ceding the city and all other conquered territories in the Caucasus back to <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>By the end of the 18th century, <a href="/wiki/Tsar" title="Tsar">Tsarist</a> Russia now began a more firm policy with the intent to conquer all of the Caucasus especially at the expense of Iran and to a lesser extent Turkey. In the spring of 1796, by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yekaterina_II" title="Yekaterina II">Yekaterina II</a>’s order, General <a href="/wiki/Valerian_Zubov" title="Valerian Zubov">Valerian Zubov</a>’s troops started a large campaign in the North Caucasus and Transcaucasia against <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Qajar</a> Persia following the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Krtsanisi" title="Battle of Krtsanisi">sack of Tblisi</a> and Iran's subsequent restoring of ts suzerainty over Georgia and <a href="/wiki/Dagestan" title="Dagestan">Dagestan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Zubov had sent 13,000 men to capture Baku, and it was overrun subsequently without any resistance. On 13 June 1796, a Russian flotilla entered Baku Bay, and a garrison of Russian troops was placed inside the city. Later, however, <a href="/wiki/Paul_I_of_Russia" title="Paul I of Russia">Pavel I</a> ordered the cessation of the campaign and the withdrawal of Russian forces following his predecessor, <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">Catherine the Great</a> her death. In March 1797, the tsarist troops left Baku and the city became part of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qajar_Iran" title="Qajar Iran">Iran</a> again.</p>
<p>In 1813, following the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1804%E2%80%9313)" title="Russo-Persian War (1804–13)">Russo-Persian War (1804–13)</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qajar_Iran" title="Qajar Iran">Qajar Iran</a> was forced to sign the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Gulistan" title="Treaty of Gulistan">Treaty of Gulistan</a> with Russia, which provided for the irrevocable cession of Baku and most of Iran's territories in the <a href="/wiki/North_Caucasus" title="North Caucasus">North Caucasus</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Caucasus" title="South Caucasus">South Caucasus</a> to Russia. However it was not until the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1826%E2%80%9328)" title="Russo-Persian War (1826–28)">Russo-Persian War (1826–28)</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Turkmenchay" title="Treaty of Turkmenchay">Treaty of Turkmenchay</a> that Baku came under nominal Russian rule and the city was irrevocably lost, as it was retaken by Iran during the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> When Baku was occupied by the Russian troops during the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1804%E2%80%9313)" title="Russo-Persian War (1804–13)">war of 1804–13</a>, nearly the entire population of some 8,000 people was ethnic <a href="/wiki/Tat_people_(Caucasus)" title="Tat people (Caucasus)">Tat</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.nl_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.nl-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Discovery_of_oil">Discovery of oil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Discovery of oil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry_in_Azerbaijan" title="Petroleum industry in Azerbaijan">Petroleum industry in Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BibiEybat.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="365" data-file-width="640" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/BibiEybat.jpg/220px-BibiEybat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/BibiEybat.jpg/330px-BibiEybat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/BibiEybat.jpg/440px-BibiEybat.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BibiEybat.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Oil workers digging an oil well by hand at Bibi-Heybat.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first <a href="/wiki/Oil_well" title="Oil well">oil well</a> was mechanically drilled in the <a href="/wiki/Bibi-Heybat_Mosque" title="Bibi-Heybat Mosque">Bibi-Heybat</a> suburb of Baku in 1846, though a number of hand-dug wells predate it. Large-scale oil exploration started in 1872, when Russian imperial authorities auctioned the parcels of oil-rich land around Baku to private investors. The pioneer of oil extracting from the bottom of the sea was Polish geologist Witold Zglenicki.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Soon after that Swiss, British, French, Belgian, German, Swedish and American investors appeared in Baku. Among them were the firms of the <a href="/wiki/Robert_Nobel" title="Robert Nobel">Nobel brothers</a> together with the family <a href="/wiki/Schuch" title="Schuch">von Börtzell-Szuch</a> (Carl Knut Börtzell, who also owned the <a href="/wiki/Livadia_Palace" title="Livadia Palace">Livadia Palace</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Rothschild_family" title="Rothschild family">Rothschild family</a>. An industrial oil belt, better known as Black City, was established near Baku.</p>
<p>Professor <a href="/wiki/A._V._Williams_Jackson" title="A. V. Williams Jackson">A. V. Williams Jackson</a> of Columbia University wrote in his work <i>From Constantinople to the Home of Omar Khayyam</i> (1911):</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Baku is a city founded upon oil, for to its inexhaustible founts of naphtha it owes its very existence, its maintenance, its prosperity.... At present Baku produces one-fifth of the oil that is used in the world, and the immense output in crude petroleum from this single city far surpasses that in any other district where oil is found. Verily, the words of the Scriptures find illustration here: 'the rock poured me out rivers of oil.</p>
<p>Oil is in the air one breathes, in one's nostrils, in one's eyes, in the water of the morning bath (though not in the drinking water, for that is brought in bottles from distant mineral springs), in one's starched linen – everywhere. This is the impression one carries away from Baku, and it is certainly true in the environs.<i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></i></p>
</blockquote>
<p>By the beginning of the 20th century almost half of world production was being extracted in Baku.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Oil_boom" title="Oil boom">oil boom</a> contributed to the massive growth of Baku. Between 1856 and 1910 Baku's population grew at a faster rate than that of <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> or <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I">World War I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: World War I">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Army_of_Azerbaijan_in_1918.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="275" data-file-width="403" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Army_of_Azerbaijan_in_1918.jpg/220px-Army_of_Azerbaijan_in_1918.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Army_of_Azerbaijan_in_1918.jpg/330px-Army_of_Azerbaijan_in_1918.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f7/Army_of_Azerbaijan_in_1918.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Army_of_Azerbaijan_in_1918.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Soldiers and officers of the army of the Azerbaijan Democratic Republic shortly after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Baku" title="Battle of Baku">Battle of Baku</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Neftchiler_Avenue_1918-1920.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="466" data-file-width="800" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Neftchiler_Avenue_1918-1920.jpg/220px-Neftchiler_Avenue_1918-1920.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Neftchiler_Avenue_1918-1920.jpg/330px-Neftchiler_Avenue_1918-1920.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Neftchiler_Avenue_1918-1920.jpg/440px-Neftchiler_Avenue_1918-1920.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Neftchiler_Avenue_1918-1920.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neftchiler_Avenue" title="Neftchiler Avenue">Neftchiler Avenue</a> in Baku, circa 1920.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1917, after the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October revolution</a> and amidst the turmoil of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_revolution" title="Russian revolution">breakup of the Russian Empire</a>, Baku came under the control of the <a href="/wiki/26_Baku_Commissars" title="26 Baku Commissars">Baku Commune</a>, which was led by veteran Bolshevik <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stepan_Shahumyan" title="Stepan Shahumyan">Stepan Shahumyan</a>. Seeking to capitalize on the existing inter-ethnic conflicts, by spring 1918, Bolsheviks inspired and condoned civil warfare in and around Baku. During the infamous <a href="/wiki/March_Days" title="March Days">March Days</a>, Bolsheviks and <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Revolutionary_Federation" title="Armenian Revolutionary Federation">Dashnaks</a> seeking to establish control over the Baku streets, were faced with armed Azerbaijani groups. The Azerbaijanis suffered a crushing defeat by the united forces of the Baku Soviet and were massacred by Dashnak teams in what was called <a href="/wiki/March_Days" title="March Days">March Days</a>. An estimated 3–12,000 Azerbaijanis were killed in their own capital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smithmusavat_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-smithmusavat-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-minahan_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-minahan-27">[27]</a></sup> After the massacre, on 28 May 1918, the Azerbaijani faction of the <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasian_Democratic_Federative_Republic" title="Transcaucasian Democratic Federative Republic">Transcaucasian Sejm</a> proclaimed the independence of the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Democratic_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Democratic Republic">Azerbaijan Democratic Republic</a> (ADR) in <a href="/wiki/Ganja,_Azerbaijan" title="Ganja, Azerbaijan">Ganja</a>, thereby becoming the first Muslim-majority <a href="/wiki/Democratic_republic" title="Democratic republic">democratic</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secular" title="Secular">secular</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The newly independent Azerbaijani republic, being unable to defend the independence of the country on their own, asked the Ottoman Empire for military support in accordance with clause 4 of the treaty between the two countries. Shortly after, Azerbaijani forces, with support of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottoman_Army_of_Islam" title="Ottoman Army of Islam">Ottoman Army of Islam</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Nuri_Killigil" title="Nuri Killigil">Nuru Pasha</a>, started their advance into Baku, eventually capturing the city from the loose coalition of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolshevik" title="Bolshevik">Bolsheviks</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socialist-Revolutionary_Party" title="Socialist-Revolutionary Party">Esers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Revolutionary_Federation" title="Armenian Revolutionary Federation">Dashnaks</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Menshevik" title="Menshevik">Mensheviks</a> and British forces under the command of General <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Dunsterville" title="Lionel Dunsterville">Lionel Dunsterville</a> on 15 September 1918.</p>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Baku" title="Battle of Baku">Battle of Baku</a>, the Azerbaijani irregular troops, with the tacit support of the Turkish command, conducted four days of pillaging and killing of 10–30,000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gen_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gen-29">[29]</a></sup> of the <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_Baku" title="Armenians in Baku">Armenian residents of Baku</a>. This pogrom was known as the <a href="/wiki/September_Days" title="September Days">September Days</a>. Shortly after this Baku was proclaimed the new capital of the Azerbaijan Democratic Republic.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_conquest">Soviet conquest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Soviet conquest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The independence of the Azerbaijani republic was a significant but a short lived chapter. On 28 April 1920, the <a href="/wiki/11th_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="11th Army (Soviet Union)">11th Red Army</a> invaded Baku and reinstalled the Bolsheviks, making Baku the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Soviet Socialist Republic">Azerbaijan Soviet Socialist Republic</a>.</p>
<p>The city underwent many major changes. As a result, Baku played a great role in many branches of the Soviet life. Since about 1921, the city was headed by the Baku City Executive Committee, commonly known in Russian as <i>Bakgorispolkom</i>. Together with the Baku Party Committee (known as the <i>Baksovet</i>), it developed the economic significance of the Caspian metropolis. From 1922 to 1930, Baku was the venue for one of the major <a href="/wiki/Trade_fair" title="Trade fair">Trade fairs</a> of the Soviet Union, serving as a commercial bridgehead to Iran and the Middle East.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Baku's growing importance as a major energy hub remained in sight of the major powers. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Case_Blue" title="Case Blue">Nazi German invasion of the southwestern Soviet Union</a>, Baku had become of vital strategic importance. In fact, capturing the <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry_in_Azerbaijan#World_War_II" title="Petroleum industry in Azerbaijan">oil fields of Baku</a> was one of the ultimate goals of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Edelweiss" title="Operation Edelweiss">Operation Edelweiss</a>, carried out between May and November 1942. However the German Army's closest approach to Baku was no closer than some 530 kilometres (329 miles) northwest of Baku in November 1942, falling far short of the city's capture before being driven back during the Soviet <a href="/wiki/Operation_Little_Saturn" title="Operation Little Saturn">Operation Little Saturn</a> in mid-December 1942.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fall_of_the_Soviet_Union_and_later">Fall of the Soviet Union and later</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Fall of the Soviet Union and later">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a>, Baku embarked on a process of restructuring on a scale unseen in its history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Thousands of buildings from the Soviet period were demolished to make way for a green belt on its shores; parks and gardens were built on the land reclaimed by filling up the beaches of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baku_Bay" title="Baku Bay">Baku Bay</a>. Improvements were made in the general cleaning, maintenance, and garbage collection, and these services are now at Western European standards. The city is growing dynamically and developing at full speed on an east-west axis along the shores of the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baku,_Azerbaijan,_satellite_image,_LandSat-5,_2010-09-06.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3826" data-file-width="4455" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Baku%2C_Azerbaijan%2C_satellite_image%2C_LandSat-5%2C_2010-09-06.jpg/220px-Baku%2C_Azerbaijan%2C_satellite_image%2C_LandSat-5%2C_2010-09-06.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Baku%2C_Azerbaijan%2C_satellite_image%2C_LandSat-5%2C_2010-09-06.jpg/330px-Baku%2C_Azerbaijan%2C_satellite_image%2C_LandSat-5%2C_2010-09-06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Baku%2C_Azerbaijan%2C_satellite_image%2C_LandSat-5%2C_2010-09-06.jpg/440px-Baku%2C_Azerbaijan%2C_satellite_image%2C_LandSat-5%2C_2010-09-06.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Baku,_Azerbaijan,_satellite_image,_LandSat-5,_2010-09-06.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Absheron Peninsular satellite image, <a href="/wiki/Landsat_5" title="Landsat 5">Landsat 5</a>, 6 September 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Baku is situated on the western coast of <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a>. In the vicinity of the city there are a number of <a href="/wiki/Mud_volcano" title="Mud volcano">mud volcanoes</a> (Keyraki, Bogkh-bogkha, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lokbatan" title="Lokbatan">Lokbatan</a> and others) and <a href="/wiki/Salt_lake" title="Salt lake">salt lakes</a> (<a href="/wiki/Lake_Boyukshor" title="Lake Boyukshor">Boyukshor</a>, Khodasan and so on).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Baku has a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperate" title="Temperate">temperate</a> <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>: <i>BSk</i>) with warm and dry summers, cool and occasionally wet winters, and strong winds all year long. However, unlike many other cities with this climate, Baku does not see extremely hot summers. This is largely because of its northerly <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a> and the fact that it is located on a peninsula on the shore of the Caspian Sea. Baku and the <a href="/wiki/Absheron_Peninsula" title="Absheron Peninsula">Absheron Peninsula</a> on which it is situated, is the most arid part of Azerbaijan (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a> here is around or less than 200 mm (8 in) a year). The majority of the light annual precipitation occurs in seasons other than summer, but none of these seasons are particularly wet. During Soviet times, Baku with its long hours of sunshine and dry healthy climate, was a vacation destination where citizens could enjoy beaches or relax in now-dilapidated <a href="/wiki/Destination_spa" title="Destination spa">spa</a> complexes overlooking the Caspian Sea. The city's past as a Soviet industrial center has left it as one of the most polluted cities in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ForbesPollution_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-ForbesPollution-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the same time Baku is noted as a very windy city throughout the year, hence the city's nickname the "<a href="/wiki/City_of_Winds" title="City of Winds">City of Winds</a>", and gale-force winds, the cold northern wind <i><a href="/wiki/Khazri" title="Khazri">khazri</a></i> and the warm southern wind <i><a href="/wiki/Gilavar" title="Gilavar">gilavar</a></i> are typical here in all seasons. Indeed, the city is renowned for its fierce winter snow storms and harsh winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Web.archive.org_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Web.archive.org-8">[8]</a></sup> The speed of the <i>khazri</i> sometimes reaches 144 kph (89 mph), which can cause damage to crops, trees and roof tiles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>The daily mean temperature in July and August averages 26.4 °C (79.5 °F), and there is very little rainfall during that season. During summer the <i>khazri</i> sweeps through, bringing desired coolness. Winter is cool and occasionally wet, with the daily mean temperature in January and February averaging 4.3 °C (39.7 °F). During winter the <i>khazri</i> sweeps through, driven by polar <a href="/wiki/Air_mass" title="Air mass">air masses</a>; temperatures on the coast frequently drop below freezing and make it feel bitterly cold. Winter <a href="/wiki/Winter_storm" title="Winter storm">snow storms</a> are occasional; <a href="/wiki/Snow" title="Snow">snow</a> usually melts within a few days after each snowfall.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Today, Baku is divided into 12 <i>rayons</i> (administrative districts) and 5 settlements of city type.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The mayor, presently <a href="/wiki/Hajibala_Abutalybov" title="Hajibala Abutalybov">Hajibala Abutalybov</a>, embodies the executive power of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Until 1988 Baku had very large Russian, Armenian, and Jewish populations which contributed to <a href="/wiki/Cultural_diversity" title="Cultural diversity">cultural diversity</a> and added in various ways (music, literature, architecture and progressive outlook) to Baku's history. With the onset of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karabakh_War" title="Karabakh War">Karabakh War</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pogrom_of_Armenians_in_Baku" title="Pogrom of Armenians in Baku">pogrom against Armenians</a> starting in January 1990, the city's large Armenian population was expelled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Under Communism, the Soviets took over the majority of Jewish property in Baku and Kuba. After the collapse of the Soviet Union, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Azerbaijan" title="President of Azerbaijan">Azerbaijani President</a> <a href="/wiki/Heydar_Aliyev" title="Heydar Aliyev">Heydar Aliyev</a> returned several synagogues and a Jewish college, nationalized by the Soviets, to the Jewish community. He encouraged the restoration of these buildings and is well liked by the Jews of Azerbaijan. Renovation has begun on seven of the original 11 synagogues, including the Gilah synagogue, built in 1896, and the large Kruei Synagogue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Christmas_in_Baku_on_January_6,_1904_and_Armenian_church.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="908" data-file-width="1400" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/89/Christmas_in_Baku_on_January_6%2C_1904_and_Armenian_church.jpg/220px-Christmas_in_Baku_on_January_6%2C_1904_and_Armenian_church.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/89/Christmas_in_Baku_on_January_6%2C_1904_and_Armenian_church.jpg/330px-Christmas_in_Baku_on_January_6%2C_1904_and_Armenian_church.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/89/Christmas_in_Baku_on_January_6%2C_1904_and_Armenian_church.jpg/440px-Christmas_in_Baku_on_January_6%2C_1904_and_Armenian_church.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Christmas_in_Baku_on_January_6,_1904_and_Armenian_church.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Armenian <a href="/wiki/Saint_Gregory_the_Illuminator%27s_Church,_Baku" title="Saint Gregory the Illuminator's Church, Baku">Saint Gregory the Illuminator's Church, Baku</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Today the vast majority of the population of Baku are ethnic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_people" title="Azerbaijani people">Azerbaijanis</a> (more than 90%). When Baku was occupied by the Russian troops during the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1804%E2%80%9313)" title="Russo-Persian War (1804–13)">war of 1804–13</a>, nearly the entire population of some 8,000 people was ethnic <a href="/wiki/Tat_people_(Caucasus)" title="Tat people (Caucasus)">Tat</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.nl_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.nl-22">[22]</a></sup> The intensive growth of the population started in the middle of the 19th century when Baku was a small town with a population of about 7,000 people. The population increased again from about 13,000 in the 1860s to 112,000 in 1897 and 215,000 in 1913, making Baku the largest city in the Caucasus region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>Baku has been a cosmopolitan city at certain times during its history, meaning ethnic Azerbaijanis did not constitute the majority of population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> In 2003 Baku additionally had 153,400 <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_person" title="Internally displaced person">internally displaced persons</a> and 93,400 refugees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bibi-Eybat_mosque,_Baku,_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1200" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Bibi-Eybat_mosque%2C_Baku%2C_2009.jpg/220px-Bibi-Eybat_mosque%2C_Baku%2C_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Bibi-Eybat_mosque%2C_Baku%2C_2009.jpg/330px-Bibi-Eybat_mosque%2C_Baku%2C_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Bibi-Eybat_mosque%2C_Baku%2C_2009.jpg/440px-Bibi-Eybat_mosque%2C_Baku%2C_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bibi-Eybat_mosque,_Baku,_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The 13th century <a href="/wiki/Bibi-Heybat_Mosque" title="Bibi-Heybat Mosque">Bibi-Heybat Mosque</a>. The mosque was built over the tomb of a descendant of <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bibi_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bibi-57">[57]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The urban landscape of Baku is shaped by many communities. The religion with the largest community of followers is Islam. The majority of the Muslims are <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia Muslims</a>, and the Republic of Azerbaijan has the second highest Shia population percentage in the world after <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The city's notable mosques include <a href="/wiki/Juma_Mosque_(Baku)" title="Juma Mosque (Baku)">Juma Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bibi-Heybat_Mosque" title="Bibi-Heybat Mosque">Bibi-Heybat Mosque</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muhammad_Mosque_(Baku)" title="Muhammad Mosque (Baku)">Muhammad Mosque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taza_Pir_Mosque" title="Taza Pir Mosque">Taza Pir Mosque</a>.</p>
<p>There are some other faiths practiced among the different ethnic groups within the country. By article 48 of its <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Azerbaijan" title="Constitution of Azerbaijan">Constitution</a>, Azerbaijan is a <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular state</a> and ensures religious freedom. Religious minorities include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church" title="Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Christians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Levantines_(Latin_Christians)" title="Levantines (Latin Christians)">Catholic Levantines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Orthodox_Church" title="Georgian Orthodox Church">Georgian Orthodox Christians</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutherans" title="Lutherans">Lutherans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_Jews" title="Azerbaijani Jews">Ashkenazi</a> Jews and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sufi" title="Sufi">Sufi</a> Muslims.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a>, although extinct in the city as well as in the rest of the country by the present time, had a long <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism_in_Azerbaijan" title="Zoroastrianism in Azerbaijan">history in Azerbaijan</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nowruz" title="Nowruz">Zoroastrian New Year</a> (Nowruz) continues to be the main holiday in the city as well as in the rest of Azerbaijan.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Baku's largest industry is petroleum, and its petroleum exports make it a large contributor to Azerbaijan's <a href="/wiki/Balance_of_payments" title="Balance of payments">balance of payments</a>. The existence of petroleum has been known since the 8th century. In the 10th century, the Arabian traveler, Marudee, reported that both white and black oil were being extracted naturally from Baku.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> By the 15th century, oil for lamps was obtained from hand-dug surface wells. Commercial exploitation began in 1872, and by the beginning of the 20th century the <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry_in_Azerbaijan" title="Petroleum industry in Azerbaijan">Baku oil fields</a> were the largest in the world. Towards the end of the 20th century much of the onshore petroleum had been exhausted, and drilling had extended into the sea offshore. By the end of the 19th century <a href="/wiki/Skilled_worker" title="Skilled worker">skilled workers</a> and specialists flocked to Baku. By 1900 the city had more than 3,000 oil wells, of which 2,000 were producing oil at industrial levels. Baku ranked as one of the largest centres for the production of <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry" title="Petroleum industry">oil industry</a> equipment before World War II. The World War II <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad" title="Battle of Stalingrad">Battle of Stalingrad</a> was fought to determine who would have control of the Baku oil fields. Fifty years before the battle, Baku produced half of the world's oil supply.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>Currently the oil economy of Baku is undergoing a resurgence, with the development of the massive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azeri%E2%80%93Chirag%E2%80%93Guneshli" title="Azeri–Chirag–Guneshli">Azeri-Chirag-Guneshli</a> field (Shallow water Gunashli by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Oil_Company_of_Azerbaijan_Republic" title="State Oil Company of Azerbaijan Republic">SOCAR</a>, deeper areas by a consortium led by <a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">BP</a>), development of the <a href="/wiki/Shah_Deniz_gas_field" title="Shah Deniz gas field">Shah Deniz gas field</a>, the expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Sangachal_Terminal" title="Sangachal Terminal">Sangachal Terminal</a> and the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Baku%E2%80%93Tbilisi%E2%80%93Ceyhan_pipeline" title="Baku–Tbilisi–Ceyhan pipeline">BTC Pipeline</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Baku_Stock_Exchange" title="Baku Stock Exchange">Baku Stock Exchange</a> is Azerbaijan's largest <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a>, and largest in the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasian</a> region by <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market capitalization</a>. A relatively large number of transnational companies are headquartered in Baku. One of the more prominent institutions headquartered in Baku is the <a href="/wiki/International_Bank_of_Azerbaijan" title="International Bank of Azerbaijan">International Bank of Azerbaijan</a>, which employs over 1,000 people. International banks with branches in Baku include <a href="/wiki/HSBC" title="HSBC">HSBC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_G%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale" title="Société Générale">Société Générale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Credit_Suisse" title="Credit Suisse">Credit Suisse</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism_and_shopping">Tourism and shopping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tourism and shopping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Baku is one of the most important tourist destinations in the Caucasus, with hotels in the city earning 7 million euros in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Many sizable world <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hotel_chain" title="Hotel chain">hotel chains</a> have a presence in the city. Baku has many popular tourist and entertainment spots, such as the downtown <a href="/wiki/Fountains_Square,_Baku" title="Fountains Square, Baku">Fountains Square</a>, the One and Thousand Nights Beach, <a href="/wiki/Shikhov_Beach" title="Shikhov Beach">Shikhov Beach</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_Rocks" title="Oil Rocks">Oil Rocks</a>. Baku's vicinities feature <a href="/wiki/Yanar_Dag" title="Yanar Dag">Yanar Dag</a>, an ever-blazing spot of natural gas. On 2 September 2010, with the inauguration of <a href="/wiki/National_Flag_Square" title="National Flag Square">National Flag Square</a>, Baku became home to the world's tallest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flagpole" title="Flagpole">flagpole</a>, according to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guinness_Book_of_Records" title="Guinness Book of Records">Guinness Book of Records</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> However, on 24 May 2011 Baku lost this record by just 3 metres (9.8 feet) to the city of Dushanbe in Tajikistan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Baku has several shopping malls; the most famous city center malls are <a href="/wiki/Park_Bulvar" title="Park Bulvar">Park Bulvar</a>, Genclik Mall, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Metro_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Metro Park (page does not exist)">Metro Park</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=28_MALL&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="28 MALL (page does not exist)">28 MALL</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Aygun_city&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Aygun city (page does not exist)">Aygun city</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=AF_MALL&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="AF MALL (page does not exist)">AF MALL</a>. The retail areas contain shops from chain stores up to high-end boutiques.</p>
<p>The city is listed 48th in the 2011 <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_cities_for_expatriate_employees" title="List of most expensive cities for expatriate employees">list</a> of the most expensive cities in the world conducted by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mercer_Human_Resource_Consulting" title="Mercer Human Resource Consulting">Mercer Human Resource Consulting</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Nizami_Street" title="Nizami Street">Nizami Street</a> is one of the most expensive streets in the world.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The city has many amenities that offer a wide range of cultural activities, drawing both from a rich local dramatic portfolio and an international repertoire. It also boasts many museums such as <a href="/wiki/Baku_Museum_of_Modern_Art" title="Baku Museum of Modern Art">Baku Museum of Modern Art</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_State_Museum_of_History" title="Azerbaijan State Museum of History">Azerbaijan State Museum of History</a>, most notably featuring historical artifacts and <a href="/wiki/Art_museum" title="Art museum">art</a>. Many of the city's cultural sites were celebrated in 2009 when Baku was designated an Islamic Culture Capital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Baku was also chosen to host the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Dance_Contest" title="Eurovision Dance Contest">Eurovision Dance Contest</a> 2010.</p>
<p>Among Baku's prestigious cultural venues are <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_State_Philharmonic_Hall" title="Azerbaijan State Philharmonic Hall">Azerbaijan State Philharmonic Hall</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_State_Academic_Opera_and_Ballet_Theatre" title="Azerbaijan State Academic Opera and Ballet Theatre">Azerbaijan State Academic Opera and Ballet Theatre</a>. The main <a href="/wiki/Movie_theater" title="Movie theater">movie theatre</a> is Azerbaijan Cinema. Festivals include the Baku International Film Festival, <a href="/wiki/Baku_International_Jazz_Festival" title="Baku International Jazz Festival">Baku International Jazz Festival</a>, Novruz Festival, <i>Gül Bayramı</i> (Flower Festival) and the National Theater Festival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> International and local exhibitions are presented at the <a href="/wiki/Baku_Expo_Center" title="Baku Expo Center">Baku Expo Center</a>.</p>
<p>As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the city along with <a href="/wiki/Ganja,_Azerbaijan" title="Ganja, Azerbaijan">Ganja</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lankaran" title="Lankaran">Lankaran</a> participates in <a href="/wiki/Earth_Hour" title="Earth Hour">Earth Hour</a> movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
