</center>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Architecture_in_Baku" title="Architecture in Baku">Architecture in Baku</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baku_Maiden_Tower_2010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="634" data-file-width="950" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Baku_Maiden_Tower_2010.jpg/220px-Baku_Maiden_Tower_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Baku_Maiden_Tower_2010.jpg/330px-Baku_Maiden_Tower_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Baku_Maiden_Tower_2010.jpg/440px-Baku_Maiden_Tower_2010.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Baku_Maiden_Tower_2010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Maiden_Tower_(Baku)" title="Maiden Tower (Baku)">Maiden Tower</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Baku" title="Old Baku">Old Baku</a>, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> built in the 11th–12th century, recognised as the symbol of the city.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Baku has wildly varying architecture, ranging from the <a href="/wiki/Old_City_(Baku)" title="Old City (Baku)">Old City</a> core to modern buildings and the spacious layout of the Baku port. Many of the city's most impressive buildings were built during the early 20th century, when architectural elements of the European styles were combined in <a href="/wiki/Eclecticism" title="Eclecticism">eclectic</a> style.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Baku thus has an original and unique appearance, earning it a reputation as the 'Paris of the East'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Late modern and postmodern architecture began to appear in the early 2000s. With economic development, old buildings such as Atlant House were razed to make way for new ones. Buildings with all-glass shells have appeared around the city, the most prominent examples being the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Tower" title="Azerbaijan Tower">Azerbaijan Tower</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heydar_Aliyev_Center" title="Heydar Aliyev Center">Heydar Aliyev Cultural Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flame_Towers" title="Flame Towers">Flame Towers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baku_Crystal_Hall" title="Baku Crystal Hall">Baku Crystal Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baku_White_City" title="Baku White City">Baku White City</a> and <a href="/wiki/SOCAR_Tower" title="SOCAR Tower">SOCAR Tower</a>. These projects also caught the attention of international media as notable programmes such as <a href="/wiki/Discovery_Channel" title="Discovery Channel">Discovery Channel</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Extreme_Engineering" title="Extreme Engineering">Extreme Engineering</a> did pieces focusing in on changes to the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Old City of Baku, also known as the Walled City of Baku, refers to the ancient Baku settlement. Most of the walls and towers, strengthened after the Russian conquest in 1806, survived. This section is picturesque, with its maze of narrow alleys and ancient buildings: the cobbled streets past the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_the_Shirvanshahs" title="Palace of the Shirvanshahs">Palace of the Shirvanshahs</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Caravanserai" title="Caravanserai">caravansaries</a>, the baths and the <a href="/wiki/Juma_Mosque_(Baku)" title="Juma Mosque (Baku)">Juma Mosque</a> (which used to house the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_National_Carpet_Museum" title="Azerbaijan National Carpet Museum">Azerbaijan National Carpet and Arts Museum</a> but is now a mosque again). The old town core also has dozens of small mosques, often without any particular sign to distinguish them as such.</p>
<p>In 2003, UNESCO placed the Inner City on the <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_in_Danger" title="List of World Heritage in Danger">List of World Heritage in Danger</a>, citing damage from a <a href="/wiki/2000_Baku_earthquake" title="2000 Baku earthquake">November 2000 earthquake</a>, poor conservation as well as "dubious" restoration efforts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_media">Music and media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Music and media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pht-Vugar_Ibadov_eurovision_(31).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2832" data-file-width="4256" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Pht-Vugar_Ibadov_eurovision_%2831%29.jpg/220px-Pht-Vugar_Ibadov_eurovision_%2831%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Pht-Vugar_Ibadov_eurovision_%2831%29.jpg/330px-Pht-Vugar_Ibadov_eurovision_%2831%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Pht-Vugar_Ibadov_eurovision_%2831%29.jpg/440px-Pht-Vugar_Ibadov_eurovision_%2831%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pht-Vugar_Ibadov_eurovision_(31).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Baku_Crystal_Hall" title="Baku Crystal Hall">Baku Crystal Hall</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2012" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2012">Eurovision Song Contest 2012</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The music scene in Baku can be traced back to ancient times and villages of Baku, generally revered as the fountainhead of <a href="/wiki/Meykhana" title="Meykhana">meykhana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mugham" title="Mugham">mugham</a> in the Azerbaijan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>In recent years, the success of Azerbaijani performers such as <a href="/wiki/Aysel_Teymurzadeh" title="Aysel Teymurzadeh">AySel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Farid_Mammadov" title="Farid Mammadov">Farid Mammadov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sabina_Babayeva" title="Sabina Babayeva">Sabina Babayeva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Safura_Alizadeh" title="Safura Alizadeh">Safura</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elnur_H%C3%BCseynov" title="Elnur Hüseynov">Elnur Hüseynov</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="Eurovision Song Contest">Eurovision Song Contest</a> has significantly boosted the profile of Baku's music scene, prompting international attention. Following the victory of Azerbaijan's representative <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eldar_%26_Nigar" title="Eldar &amp; Nigar">Eldar &amp; Nigar</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2011" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2011">Eurovision Song Contest 2011</a>, Baku hosted the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2012" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2012">Eurovision Song Contest 2012</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>2005 was a landmark in the development of <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_jazz" title="Azerbaijani jazz">Azerbaijani jazz</a> in the city. It has been home to legendary jazz musicians like <a href="/wiki/Vagif_Mustafazadeh" title="Vagif Mustafazadeh">Vagif Mustafazadeh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aziza_Mustafa_Zadeh" title="Aziza Mustafa Zadeh">Aziza Mustafa Zadeh</a>, Rafig Babayev and Rain Sultanov.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Among Baku's prominent annual fairs and festivals is <a href="/wiki/Baku_International_Jazz_Festival" title="Baku International Jazz Festival">Baku International Jazz Festival</a>, which features some of the world's most identifiable jazz names.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>Baku also has a thriving <a href="/wiki/Mugham" title="Mugham">International Center of Mugham</a>, which is located in <a href="/wiki/Baku_Boulevard" title="Baku Boulevard">Baku Boulevard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gulustan_Palace" title="Gulustan Palace">Gulustan Palace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buta_Palace" title="Buta Palace">Buta Palace</a>, one of the principal <a href="/wiki/Performing_arts_center" title="Performing arts center">performing arts centers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Music_venue" title="Music venue">music venues</a> in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>The majority of Azerbaijan's media companies (including television, newspaper and radio, such as <a href="/wiki/ANS_TV" title="ANS TV">ANS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azad_Azerbaijan_TV" title="Azad Azerbaijan TV">Azad Azerbaijan TV</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ictimai_TV" title="Ictimai TV">Ictimai TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lider_TV" title="Lider TV">Lider TV</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Region_TV" title="Region TV">Region TV</a>) are headquartered in Baku. The films <i><a href="/wiki/The_World_Is_Not_Enough" title="The World Is Not Enough">The World Is Not Enough</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Diamond_Arm" title="The Diamond Arm">The Diamond Arm</a></i> are set in the city, while <i><a href="/wiki/Amphibian_Man_(film)" title="Amphibian Man (film)">Amphibian Man</a></i> includes several scenes filmed in <a href="/wiki/Old_City_(Baku)" title="Old City (Baku)">Old City</a>.</p>
<p>Out of the city's radio stations <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ANS_ChM" title="ANS ChM">ANS ChM</a>, <i>Ictimai Radio</i>, <i>Radio Antenn</i>, <i>Burc FM</i>, and <i>Lider FM Jazz</i> are some of the more influential competitors with large national audiences. ANS ChM was one of the first private and independent <a href="/wiki/FM_broadcasting" title="FM broadcasting">FM radio</a> broadcasting service in the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> and Central Asia regions when it was established in May 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-undp_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-undp-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some of the most influential Baku newspapers include the daily <i><a href="/wiki/Azadliq_(newspaper)" title="Azadliq (newspaper)">Azadliq</a></i>, <i>Zaman</i> (The Time), <i>Bakinskiy Rabochiy</i> (The Baku Worker), <i><a href="/wiki/Echo_(Azerbaijani_newspaper)" title="Echo (Azerbaijani newspaper)">Echo</a></i> and the English-language <i>Baku Today</i>.</p>
<p>Baku is also featured in the video game <i><a href="/wiki/Battlefield_4" title="Battlefield 4">Battlefield 4</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nightlife">Nightlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Nightlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Baku boasts a vibrant nightlife. Many clubs that are open until dawn can be found throughout the city. Clubs with an eastern flavor provide special treats from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Azerbaijan" title="Cuisine of Azerbaijan">cuisine of Azerbaijan</a> along with local music. Western-style clubs target younger, more energetic crowds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Most of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_house" title="Public house">public houses</a> and bars are located near <a href="/wiki/Fountains_Square,_Baku" title="Fountains Square, Baku">Fountains Square</a> and are usually open until the early hours of the morning.</p>
<p>Baku is home to restaurants catering to every cuisine and occasion. Restaurants range from luxurious and expensive to ordinary and affordable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Lonely_Planet" title="Lonely Planet">Lonely Planet</a> "1000 Ultimate Experiences", Baku placed 8th among the top 10 party cities in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nl_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-nl-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_gardens">Parks and gardens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Parks and gardens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Panoramabild_Baku_Filarmonia_Park.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="732" data-file-width="2069" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Panoramabild_Baku_Filarmonia_Park.JPG/350px-Panoramabild_Baku_Filarmonia_Park.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Panoramabild_Baku_Filarmonia_Park.JPG/525px-Panoramabild_Baku_Filarmonia_Park.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Panoramabild_Baku_Filarmonia_Park.JPG/700px-Panoramabild_Baku_Filarmonia_Park.JPG 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Panoramabild_Baku_Filarmonia_Park.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<center>Philarmony garden</center>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Baku has large sections of greenery either preserved by the National Government or designated as green zones. The city, however, continues to lack a green belt development as economic activity pours into the capital, resulting in massive housing projects along the suburbs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Baku_Boulevard" title="Baku Boulevard">Baku Boulevard</a> is a pedestrian promenade that runs parallel to Baku's seafront. The boulevard contains an amusement park, <a href="/wiki/Yacht_club" title="Yacht club">yacht club</a>, <a href="/wiki/Musical_fountain" title="Musical fountain">musical fountain</a>, statues and monuments. The park is popular with dog-walkers and joggers, and is convenient for tourists. It is adjacent to the newly built <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Mugam_Center_of_Azerbaijan" title="International Mugam Center of Azerbaijan">International Center of Mugham</a> and the musical fountain.</p>
<p>Other prominent parks and gardens include Heydar Aliyev Park, Samad Vurgun Park, Narimanov Park, <a href="/wiki/Alley_of_Honor" title="Alley of Honor">Alley of Honor</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Fountains_Square,_Baku" title="Fountains Square, Baku">Fountains Square</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Martyrs%27_Lane" title="Martyrs' Lane">Martyrs' Lane</a>, formerly the Kirov Park, is dedicated to the memory of those who lost their lives during the <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_War" title="Nagorno-Karabakh War">Nagorno-Karabakh War</a> and also to the 137 people killed on <a href="/wiki/Black_January" title="Black January">Black January</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bedii_Gimnastika_026.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="560" data-file-width="440" height="280" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Bedii_Gimnastika_026.jpg/220px-Bedii_Gimnastika_026.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Bedii_Gimnastika_026.jpg/330px-Bedii_Gimnastika_026.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fe/Bedii_Gimnastika_026.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bedii_Gimnastika_026.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Heydar_Aliyev_Sports_and_Exhibition_Complex" title="Heydar Aliyev Sports and Exhibition Complex">Heydar Aliyev Sports and Exhibition Complex</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2009_Rhythmic_Gymnastics_European_Championships" title="2009 Rhythmic Gymnastics European Championships">2009 Rhythmic Gymnastics European Championships</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Baku hosts a <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> race through on the <a href="/wiki/Baku_City_Circuit" title="Baku City Circuit">Baku City Circuit</a>. The first was the <a href="/wiki/2016_European_Grand_Prix" title="2016 European Grand Prix">2016 European Grand Prix</a>.</p>
<p>The city will also host three group games and one quarter-final of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2020" title="UEFA Euro 2020">UEFA Euro 2020</a> European Football Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since 2002, Baku has hosted 36 major sporting events and selected to host the <a href="/wiki/2015_European_Games" title="2015 European Games">2015 European Games</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Baku is also to host the <a href="/wiki/2017_Islamic_Solidarity_Games" title="2017 Islamic Solidarity Games">fourth edition</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Solidarity_Games" title="Islamic Solidarity Games">Islamic Solidarity Games</a> in 2017.</p>
<p>Baku is also one of world's leading chess centres, having produced famous <a href="/wiki/Grandmaster_(chess)" title="Grandmaster (chess)">grandmasters</a> like <a href="/wiki/Teimour_Radjabov" title="Teimour Radjabov">Teimour Radjabov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vugar_Gashimov" title="Vugar Gashimov">Vugar Gashimov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garry_Kasparov" title="Garry Kasparov">Garry Kasparov</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shahriyar_Mammadyarov" title="Shahriyar Mammadyarov">Shahriyar Mammadyarov</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rauf_Mammadov" title="Rauf Mammadov">Rauf Mammadov</a>, as well as the arbiter <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faik_Hasanov" title="Faik Hasanov">Faik Hasanov</a>. The city also annually hosts the international tournaments such as Baku Chess Grand Prix, President's Cup, Baku Open and currently bidding to host <a href="/wiki/42nd_Chess_Olympiad" title="42nd Chess Olympiad">42nd Chess Olympiad</a> in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>First class sporting facilities were built for the indoor games, including the Palace of Hand Games and <a href="/wiki/Heydar_Aliyev_Sports_and_Exhibition_Complex" title="Heydar Aliyev Sports and Exhibition Complex">Heydar Aliyev Sports and Exhibition Complex</a>. It hosted many sporting events, including <a href="/wiki/FIFA_U-17_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="FIFA U-17 Women's World Cup">FIFA U-17 Women's World Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhythmic_Gymnastics_European_Championships" title="Rhythmic Gymnastics European Championships">Rhythmic Gymnastics European Championships</a> in <a href="/wiki/2007_Rhythmic_Gymnastics_European_Championships" title="2007 Rhythmic Gymnastics European Championships">2007</a> and <a href="/wiki/2009_Rhythmic_Gymnastics_European_Championships" title="2009 Rhythmic Gymnastics European Championships">2009</a>, <a href="/wiki/2005_World_Rhythmic_Gymnastics_Championships" title="2005 World Rhythmic Gymnastics Championships">2005 World Rhythmic Gymnastics Championships</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2007_FILA_Wrestling_World_Championships" title="2007 FILA Wrestling World Championships">2007 FILA Wrestling World Championships</a> and <a href="/wiki/2010_European_Wrestling_Championships" title="2010 European Wrestling Championships">2010 European Wrestling Championships</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_World_Amateur_Boxing_Championships" title="2011 World Amateur Boxing Championships">2011 World Amateur Boxing Championships</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Women%27s_Challenge_Cup_(volleyball)" title="Women's Challenge Cup (volleyball)">2009 Women's Challenge Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Taekwondo_Championships" title="European Taekwondo Championships">European Taekwondo Championships</a> in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Since 2011 the city annually hosts <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Tennis_Association" title="Women's Tennis Association">WTA</a> tennis event called <a href="/wiki/Baku_Cup" title="Baku Cup">Baku Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Synergy_Baku_Cycling_Project" title="Synergy Baku Cycling Project">Synergy Baku Cycling Project</a> participates in the <a href="/wiki/Tour_d%27Azerba%C3%AFdjan" title="Tour d'Azerbaïdjan">Tour d'Azerbaïdjan</a> a 2.2 multi-stage bicycle race on the UCI Europe Tour.</p>
<p>Baku made a bid to host the <a href="/wiki/Baku_bid_for_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Baku bid for the 2016 Summer Olympics">2016 Summer Olympics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baku_bid_for_the_2020_Summer_Olympics" title="Baku bid for the 2020 Summer Olympics">2020 Summer Olympics</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> but failed to become a Candidate City both times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>The largest sport hub in the city is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baku_Olympic_Stadium" title="Baku Olympic Stadium">Baku Olympic Stadium</a> with 68,700 seating capacity whose construction was completed in 2015. The city's three main football clubs are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neftchi_Baku_PFK" title="Neftchi Baku PFK">Neftchi Baku</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inter_Baku" title="Inter Baku">Inter Baku</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Baku" title="FC Baku">FC Baku</a> of whom first has eight Premier League titles making Neftchi the most successful Azerbaijani football club. Baku also has several football clubs in the premier and regional leagues, including <a href="/wiki/AZAL_PFK" title="AZAL PFK">AZAL</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ravan_Baku_FK" title="Ravan Baku FK">Ravan</a> in <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Premier_League" title="Azerbaijan Premier League">Premier League</a>. The city's second largest stadium, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tofiq_Bahramov_Stadium" title="Tofiq Bahramov Stadium">Tofiq Bahramov Stadium</a> hosts a number of domestic and international competitions and was the main sport centre of the city for a long period until the construction of Baku Olympic Stadium.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Women%27s_Volleyball_Super_League" title="Azerbaijan Women's Volleyball Super League">Azerbaijan Women's Volleyball Super League</a>, Baku is represented by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rabita_Baku" title="Rabita Baku">Rabita Baku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerrail_Baku" title="Azerrail Baku">Azerrail Baku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lokomotiv_Baku" title="Lokomotiv Baku">Lokomotiv Baku</a> and <a href="/wiki/Azeryol_Baku" title="Azeryol Baku">Azeryol Baku</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bakutaxi.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="667" data-file-width="1000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Bakutaxi.jpg/220px-Bakutaxi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Bakutaxi.jpg/330px-Bakutaxi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Bakutaxi.jpg/440px-Bakutaxi.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bakutaxi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Baku <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_cab" title="Black cab">black cab</a>, introduced in 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_car_of_the_Baku_funicular_station.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4039" data-file-width="2635" height="337" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/The_car_of_the_Baku_funicular_station.jpg/220px-The_car_of_the_Baku_funicular_station.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/The_car_of_the_Baku_funicular_station.jpg/330px-The_car_of_the_Baku_funicular_station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/The_car_of_the_Baku_funicular_station.jpg/440px-The_car_of_the_Baku_funicular_station.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_car_of_the_Baku_funicular_station.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The car of the <a href="/wiki/Baku_Funicular" title="Baku Funicular">Baku Funicular</a> station</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Throughout history the transport system of Baku used the now-defunct <a href="/wiki/Horsecar" title="Horsecar">horsecars</a>, trams and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Narrow_gauge_railways" title="Narrow gauge railways">narrow gauge railways</a>. As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 1,000 <a href="/wiki/Hackney_carriage" title="Hackney carriage">black cabs</a> are ordered by Baku Taxi Company, and as part of a programme originally announced by the Transport Ministry of Azerbaijan, there is a plan to introduce London cabs into Baku.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The move was part of £16 million agreement between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manganese_Bronze" title="Manganese Bronze">Manganese Bronze</a> and Baku Taxi Company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>Local rail transport includes the <a href="/wiki/Baku_Funicular" title="Baku Funicular">Baku Funicular</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Baku_Metro" title="Baku Metro">Baku Metro</a>, a rapid-transit system notable for its art, murals, mosaics and ornate chandeliers. Baku Metro was opened in November 1967 and includes 3 lines and 25 stations at present; 170 million people used Baku Metro over the past five years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> In 2008, the Chief of the Baku Metro, Taghi Ahmadov, announced plans to construct 41 new stations over the next 17 years. These will serve the new <a href="/wiki/Baku_International_Bus_Terminal" title="Baku International Bus Terminal">bus complex</a> as well as the international airport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>Plans are afoot to introduce a single Smart Card for payment on all types of city transport. The metro is now the only form of transport in Baku to use any type of card-based fare-payment system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>Baku's <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Railways" title="Azerbaijan Railways">Central Railway Station</a> is the terminus for national and international rail links to the city. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kars%E2%80%93Tbilisi%E2%80%93Baku_railway" title="Kars–Tbilisi–Baku railway">Kars–Tbilisi–Baku railway</a>, which will directly connect <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, Georgia and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, began to be constructed in 2007 and is scheduled for completion in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> The completed branch will connect Baku with <a href="/wiki/Tbilisi" title="Tbilisi">Tbilisi</a> in Georgia, and from there trains will continue to <a href="/wiki/Akhalkalaki" title="Akhalkalaki">Akhalkalaki</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kars" title="Kars">Kars</a> in Turkey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yacht_clubs_in_Baku.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="862" data-file-width="1866" height="102" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Yacht_clubs_in_Baku.jpg/220px-Yacht_clubs_in_Baku.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Yacht_clubs_in_Baku.jpg/330px-Yacht_clubs_in_Baku.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Yacht_clubs_in_Baku.jpg/440px-Yacht_clubs_in_Baku.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yacht_clubs_in_Baku.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Baku Yacht Club</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Sea transport is vital for Baku, as the city is practically surrounded by the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> to the east. Shipping services operate regularly from Baku across the Caspian Sea to <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrkmenba%C5%9Fy,_Turkmenistan" title="Türkmenbaşy, Turkmenistan">Turkmenbashi</a> (formerly Krasnovodsk) in <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a> and to <a href="/wiki/Bandar-e_Anzali" title="Bandar-e Anzali">Bandar Anzali</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nowshahr" title="Nowshahr">Bandar Nowshar</a> in Iran.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> The commuter ferries, along with the high-speed catamaran <i>Seabus</i> (<i>Deniz Avtobusu</i>), also form the main connection between the city and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Absheron_peninsula" title="Absheron peninsula">Absheron peninsula</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Baku Port was founded in 1902 and since then has been the largest Caspian Sea port. It has six facilities: the main cargo terminal, the container terminal, the ferry terminal, the oil terminal, the passenger terminal and the port fleet terminal. The port's throughput capacity reaches 15 million <a href="/wiki/Ton" title="Ton">tons</a> of liquid bulk and up to 10 million tons of dry cargoes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Beginning in 2010, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baku_International_Sea_Trade_Port" title="Baku International Sea Trade Port">Baku International Sea Trade Port</a> is being reconstructed. The construction will take place in three stages and will be completed by 2016. The estimated costs are 400 Million US$.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> From April to November the Baku Port is accessible to ships loading cargoes for direct voyages from Western European and Mediterranean ports. The State Road M-1 and the <a href="/wiki/European_route_E60" title="European route E60">European route E60</a> are the two main motorway connections between Europe and Azerbaijan. The motorway network around Baku is well developed and is constantly being extended. The <a href="/wiki/Heydar_Aliyev_International_Airport" title="Heydar Aliyev International Airport">Heydar Aliyev International Airport</a> is the only commercial airport serving Baku. The new <a href="/wiki/Baku_Cargo_Terminal" title="Baku Cargo Terminal">Baku Cargo Terminal</a> was officially opened in March 2005. It was constructed to be a major cargo hub in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">CIS</a> countries and is actually now one of the biggest and most technically advanced in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> There are also several smaller <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_airbase" title="Military airbase">military airbases</a> near Baku, such as <a href="/wiki/Baku_Kala_Air_Base" title="Baku Kala Air Base">Baku Kala Air Base</a>, intended for private aircraft, <a href="/wiki/Helicopter" title="Helicopter">helicopters</a> and charters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Baku" title="List of universities in Baku">List of universities in Baku</a></div>
<p>Baku hosts many universities, junior colleges and vocational schools. <a href="/wiki/Baku_State_University" title="Baku State University">Baku State University</a>, the first established university in Azerbaijan was opened in 1919 by the government of the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Democratic_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Democratic Republic">Azerbaijan Democratic Republic</a>. In the early years of the Soviet era, Baku already had <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_State_Oil_Academy" title="Azerbaijan State Oil Academy">Azerbaijan State Oil Academy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Medical_University" title="Azerbaijan Medical University">Azerbaijan Medical University</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_State_Economic_University" title="Azerbaijan State Economic University">Azerbaijan State Economic University</a>. In the post-WWII period, a few more universities were established such as <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Technical_University" title="Azerbaijan Technical University">Azerbaijan Technical University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_University_of_Languages" title="Azerbaijan University of Languages">Azerbaijan University of Languages</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Architecture_and_Construction_University" title="Azerbaijan Architecture and Construction University">Azerbaijan Architecture and Construction University</a>. After 1991 when Azerbaijan gained independence from the Soviet Union, the fall of communism led to the development of a number of private institutions, including <a href="/wiki/Qafqaz_University" title="Qafqaz University">Qafqaz University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Khazar_University" title="Khazar University">Khazar University</a> which are currently considered the most prestigious academic institutions. Apart from the private universities, the government established the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Public_Administration_(Azerbaijan)" title="Academy of Public Administration (Azerbaijan)">Academy of Public Administration</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Diplomatic_Academy" title="Azerbaijan Diplomatic Academy">Azerbaijan Diplomatic Academy</a> and various military academies. The largest universities according to the student population are Baku State University and Azerbaijan State Economic University. In addition, there are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baku_Music_Academy" title="Baku Music Academy">Baku Music Academy</a> and the Azerbaijan National Conservatoire in Baku established in the early 1920s. Publicly run kindergartens and elementary schools (years 1 through 11) are operated by local wards or municipal offices.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Azerbaijan National Academy of Sciences">Azerbaijan National Academy of Sciences</a>, the main state research organization in Azerbaijan is locating in Baku as well. Moreover, Baku has numerous libraries, many of which contain vast collections of historic documents from the Roman, Byzantine, Ottoman and Soviet periods, as well as from other civilisations of the past. The most important libraries in terms of historic document collections include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nizami_Museum_of_Azerbaijan_Literature" title="Nizami Museum of Azerbaijan Literature">Nizami Museum of Azerbaijan Literature</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Azerbaijan" title="National Library of Azerbaijan">National Library of Azerbaijan</a>, the Mirza Alakbar Central Library, the Samad Vurgun Library and the Baku Presidential Library.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care">Health care</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Health care">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The city has many public and private hospitals, clinics and laboratories within its bounds and numerous medical research centers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Many of these facilities have <a href="/wiki/High_tech" title="High tech">high technology</a> equipment, which has contributed to the recent upsurge in "<a href="/wiki/Medical_tourism" title="Medical tourism">medical tourism</a>" to Baku, particularly from post-Soviet countries such as <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a>, whose governments send lower-income patients to the city for inexpensive high-tech medical treatments and operations.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_residents">Notable residents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Notable residents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Baku" title="List of people from Baku">List of people from Baku</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/Category:People_from_Baku" title="Category:People from Baku">Category:People from Baku</a>.</div>
<p>Because of its intermittent periods of great prosperity as well as being the largest city in the Caucasus and one of the most ethnically and culturally diverse in the Soviet Union, Baku prides itself on having produced a disproportionate number of notable figures in the sciences, arts and other fields. Some of the houses they resided in display commemorative plaques. Some of the many prestigious residents include: Academy Award winners <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rustam_Ibrahimbeyov" title="Rustam Ibrahimbeyov">Rustam Ibrahimbeyov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Menshov" title="Vladimir Menshov">Vladimir Menshov</a>, one of the founders and head of the Soviet space program <a href="/wiki/Kerim_Kerimov" title="Kerim Kerimov">Kerim Kerimov</a>, Nobel Prize winner and physicist <a href="/wiki/Lev_Landau" title="Lev Landau">Lev Landau</a> and famous musicians such as <a href="/wiki/Gara_Garayev" title="Gara Garayev">Gara Garayev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uzeyir_Hajibeyov" title="Uzeyir Hajibeyov">Uzeyir Hajibeyov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Magomayev_(musician)" title="Muslim Magomayev (musician)">Muslim Magomayev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vagif_Mustafazadeh" title="Vagif Mustafazadeh">Vagif Mustafazadeh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alim_Qasimov" title="Alim Qasimov">Alim Qasimov</a>. World-famous cellist <a href="/wiki/Mstislav_Rostropovich" title="Mstislav Rostropovich">Mstislav Rostropovich</a> was born and raised in Baku, as was world-famous chess player, <a href="/wiki/Garry_Kasparov" title="Garry Kasparov">Garry Kasparov</a>.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Partner_cities">Partner cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Partner cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aberdeen" title="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a>, Scotland</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a>, Germany<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Azerbaijan_twinnings_116-9"><a href="#cite_note-Azerbaijan_twinnings-116">[116]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stavanger" title="Stavanger">Stavanger</a>, Norway</li>
</ul>
<p>Partnership relations also exist at different levels with:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Berlin, Paris, <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tbilisi" title="Tbilisi">Tbilisi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Astana" title="Astana">Astana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a>, Moscow, <a href="/wiki/Volgograd" title="Volgograd">Volgograd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kizlyar" title="Kizlyar">Kizlyar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tashkent" title="Tashkent">Tashkent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chengdu" title="Chengdu">Chengdu</a>.</p>

<tr>
<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2" style="padding:0.5em 0 0.3em; line-height:1.3em;">
<div><b>*</b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transcontinental_country" title="Transcontinental country">Transcontinental country</a>.<br/>
<b>†</b> See: <a href="/wiki/Positions_on_Jerusalem" title="Positions on Jerusalem">Positions on Jerusalem</a>. Both Israel and Palestinians claim Jerusalem as capital. <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> contains the Israeli parliament and almost all Israeli government ministries. <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a> contains most foreign embassies in Israel; <a href="/wiki/Ramallah" title="Ramallah">Ramallah</a> is the administrative seat of the Palestinian Authority.<br/>
<b>+</b> According to the 1947 <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="Constitution of the Republic of China">Constitution of the Republic of China</a>, Nanjing is the official capital of the ROC, with Taipei as the <a href="/wiki/Temporary_capital" title="Temporary capital">seat of government</a>. See also <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Taiwan" title="Political status of Taiwan">Political status of Taiwan</a>.</div>
